{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:27","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:27","title":"How to Decorate an Apartment for Cheap","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>You don't need a ton of money to decorate your apartment in style! There are many creative ways you can save on new decor and some simple tweaks you can make yourself to revamp pieces you already own for little to no cost. Drastically transforming your space without breaking the bank is completely doable. Best of all, it's fun! </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Walls and Windows\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Walls-and-Windows\">Walls and Windows</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Use removable wallpaper or decals to add style to blank walls. Most landlords don’t want renters to paint walls or install wallpaper, but that doesn’t have to cramp your style. Removable wallpaper and decals are affordable, easy to apply, and won’t damage the walls when you remove them. Check out local big box or department stores for cool options.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-1.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Decorate an Apartment for Cheap Step 1.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/aa/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-1.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-1.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For a graphic element, look for artistic decals like flowers, birds, graffiti art, symbols, and even text.</li> \n    <li>Cover one of the walls with removable wallpaper in a fun print or a colorful pattern to transform a room.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Hang or prop up a thrift store mirror to make your space feel bigger. Mirrors help light bounce around the room, creating a larger visual space.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup> The bigger the mirror, the bigger the impact! If you can’t put nails in your walls, leaning the mirror against a wall will create the same effect.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Decorate an Apartment for Cheap Step 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e2/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-2.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you don’t already have a mirror you can use, check out resale and vintage shops for a low-cost option. Look for something with a cool frame to add even more style.</li> \n    <li>Try placing the mirror over a piece of furniture, like an entry console, buffet cabinet, or even a dresser. An oversized floor mirror is also a great addition to a room if you have space.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Upgrade windows by replacing boring blinds with something stylish. Most new apartments come with plain, white plastic blinds. Switching out the window treatments doesn’t have to be costly and the difference it can make is huge. For example, try replacing the blinds with striped Roman shades or flowing statement curtains.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-3.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Decorate an Apartment for Cheap Step 3.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/25/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-3.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-3.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Hanging your curtains higher up makes your ceilings look higher. Install the curtain rods closer to the ceiling and add flowing drapes that reach the floor for a posh look.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup></li> \n    <li>If your apartment is on the smaller side, use mostly light colors for your walls, curtains, and furniture. That way, your space will feel more open and airy.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Color-code your bookshelves for a no-cost way to revamp wall space. If you’re an avid reader, bookshelves are probably taking up a lot of your wall space. Use that to your advantage by turning your bookshelves into art! Grouping and shelving your books by the color of their spines is a cool way to create style without spending a dime.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Decorate an Apartment for Cheap Step 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/27/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-4.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, try a rainbow color scheme, create a pattern, or emphasize your favorite colors by putting them front and center.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Create a statement wall by hanging large-scale thrift store artwork. Check out thrift stores, flea markets, and resale shops for colorful abstract paintings that vibe with your current color scheme. If prints are more your style, look for something large-scale and add a cool frame to take the piece to the next level.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Decorate an Apartment for Cheap Step 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b3/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-5.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you have artist friends, consider going that route instead. That way, you can rep your friends' work and get cool pieces of art for cheap (or even free).</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Furniture and Floors\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Furniture-and-Floors\">Furniture and Floors</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Add a few colorful rugs to make a statement without spending a ton. A few new rugs won’t set you back much and they can add a lot of color and energy to your space. If you’re working with existing décor, choose rugs with colors and patterns that complement it. If your space and décor are pretty neutral, a vibrant rug can be an awesome statement item.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Decorate an Apartment for Cheap Step 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/4f/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-6.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Area rugs tend to be the most expensive kind, so check out thrift stores and resale shops for those.</li> \n    <li>Smaller rugs are usually much cheaper—check out what your local big box and department stores have in stock. You may find some good deals online, too.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Breathe new life into existing furniture by repainting it. Adding a new coat of paint or finish to an old dresser, coffee table, desk, or bookshelf can drastically how they look. Remove all of the hardware, sand the piece down, and wipe off the dust. Then, brush on the new paint or spray paint it any color you want. Add a final coat of polyurethane to make the new paint last.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Decorate an Apartment for Cheap Step 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/41/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-7.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, paint your boring old desk a vibrant shade of blue-green to match the décor in your bedroom.</li> \n    <li>A new coat of stain is also a great option for wood pieces. Apply a dark wood stain to make an old piece look more expensive.</li> \n    <li>Try using multi-function furniture pieces to make the most of your space.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup> For instance, you might have a coffee table that doubles as storage.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Switch out the doorknob and furniture hardware to spruce things up. New doorknobs and furniture hardware can provide a serious style upgrade. You can pick up attractive knob and hardware replacements for pretty cheap at home improvement or big box stores. There are loads of options and styles, so shop around until you find the perfect replacements.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-8.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Decorate an Apartment for Cheap Step 8.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/48/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-8.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-8.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Remove and replace existing hardware with a simple screwdriver or electric drill.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Pick up an accent piece at a thrift store to add a unique twist to a room. Thrift stores and flea markets can be treasure troves if you want some unique and affordable furniture. Shop around at your local second-hand shops for funky coffee tables, nightstands, chairs, stools, and whatever else you need.<sup id=\"_ref-16\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 16\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-16\">[16]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-9.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Decorate an Apartment for Cheap Step 9.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/6d/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-9.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-9.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Keep in mind that you can repaint a piece and swap out the fixtures to make it even cooler for very little money. Try to look past the dull finish or weird paint and imagine its potential!</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Lighting and Fixtures\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Lighting-and-Fixtures\">Lighting and Fixtures</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Update your lamp shades to refresh your space on the cheap. Lamp shades tend to collect dust and grime, and older styles can make a space feel dated. The lamp base is the part that costs the most, so keep the bases you have, toss the old shades, and replace them with new shades. This is an easy way to add a pop of color to any room.<sup id=\"_ref-17\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 17\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-17\">[17]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-10.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Decorate an Apartment for Cheap Step 10.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c9/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-10.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-10.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>New lamp shades are pretty affordable, but thrift stores and vintage shops may have some pretty unique options.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Replace the current lighting fixtures with more stylish ones. The overhead lighting fixtures in apartments can be pretty blah or even downright ugly. You can pick up nicer ones at most home improvement stores without spending a ton of cash and they’re usually easy to swap out on your own. There are loads of styles available, so think about what vibe you’re trying to create before you hit the stores.<sup id=\"_ref-18\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 18\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-18\">[18]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Decorate an Apartment for Cheap Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/ef/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-11.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, replacing that dull overhead light in your entryway with a hanging crystal fixture can seriously upgrade the space.</li> \n    <li>Keep the old fixtures somewhere safe so you can put them back whenever you move out. Take your cool fixtures with you when you go!</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Update your dated ceiling fans with modern replacements. Most apartments have old ceiling fans or brand-new ones that look super cheap. Swap out those eye-sores for more modern options to quickly and easily give your space some pizzazz. Just remember to keep the original fan so you can reinstall it before you move out.<sup id=\"_ref-19\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 19\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-19\">[19]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-12.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Decorate an Apartment for Cheap Step 12.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/04/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-12.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-12.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>New ceiling fixtures can get pricey, but you can find affordable options online and at home improvement, big box, and discount stores.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Where to Shop\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Where-to-Shop\">Where to Shop</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Head to vintage stores to find affordable decor with personality. Local antique shops and online sources that deal in vintage can be gold mines for unique items with low price tags. Well-worn pieces gel nicely if you're going for a cozy, rustic vibe, but you can always repaint or refinish a piece to match your decor or give it a more modern feel.<sup id=\"_ref-20\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 20\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-20\">[20]</a></sup> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Shop for interesting wall art, unique coffee tables, or cool book shelves at vintage shops.</li> \n    <li>If you like to decorate with knick-knacks, vintage shops usually offer an amazing selection.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Look through local thrift stores for neat stuff at rock-bottom prices. Some vintage stores and items can be pricey, but you can always count on thrift shops for amazing deals. You may need to do a little digging to find hidden gems, so make a day of it and have fun searching through a wealth of odds and ends.<sup id=\"_ref-21\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 21\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-21\">[21]</a></sup> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Be on the lookout for quirky items and fun accessories!</li> \n    <li>If you're thinking about buying anything with electrical components, ask a store clerk to direct you to a power outlet so you can make sure it functions properly.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Wait for department store sales to grab pricey pieces on the cheap. Most department stores, major retailers, and big box stores have at least one annual sale, so ask a store clerk or check the store's website to see when their next big sale is.<sup id=\"_ref-22\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 22\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-22\">[22]</a></sup> In the meantime, check out their clearance racks for cool stuff you can take home today.<sup id=\"_ref-23\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 23\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-23\">[23]</a></sup> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Items usually go on clearance once the store's new season of decor comes in. You can find good stuff that people paid full price for just a few months ago.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Check out discount and overstock stores for cheap designer pieces. Look online and locally for discount stores that carry overstocked items at super low prices. You'll need to do some digging and hunting, but you just might find a high-end or designer piece for a fraction of the original price.<sup id=\"_ref-24\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 24\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-24\">[24]</a></sup> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Shop for multi-use pieces to get even more bang for your buck! For example, a stylish ottoman with storage space on the inside for magazines and books.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Explore the children's department at major retailers for lower prices. Bigger brands and retailers often have a section with decor for kids' rooms and you can find some pretty cool stuff there! The style and quality won't be a huge step down from the \"adult\" versions, but the prices are usually much lower.<sup id=\"_ref-25\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 25\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap#_note-25\">[25]</a></sup> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Look for items like lamps, throw pillows, and area rugs that fit your apartment's aesthetic.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Don't forget about hand-me-downs! If a family member offers you a free piece of furniture or decor, consider taking it. Try to imagine what the piece would look like with a fresh coat of paint and some stylish new hardware.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: ecorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-7.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-7.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn95@2020_4/2020/10/12/17-04-49-271_c247a677d68ab145.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/48/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-8.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-8.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn55@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-47-184_761af6b64f65308e.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/6d/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-9.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-9.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn80@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-04-49-756_1feae48fd6adb328.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c9/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-10.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-10.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn91@2020_4/2020/10/12/17-04-47-358_5f9a2bc576e6ba2e.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/ef/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-11.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-11.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn28@2020_4/2020/10/12/17-04-48-582_6c4b38cb85641016.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/04/Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-12.jpg/aid12185484-v4-728px-Decorate-an-Apartment-for-Cheap-Step-12.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn63@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-49-121_3cd65c023483ac1f.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522267297},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:27","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:27","title":"How to Cook Asparagus Tips","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Asparagus is a tasty and healthy vegetable that goes with almost any meal. You’re probably used to seeing whole stalks, but can you eat the tips? You sure can! In fact, asparagus tips are the tastiest and most tender parts of the whole plant. Better yet, cooking the tips is basically the same as cooking the stalks. Simply cut off the tips and try out one of these recipes for a delicious and nutritious side dish. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Asparagus-Tips&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Asparagus-Tips&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Prepping the Asparagus\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Prepping-the-Asparagus\">Prepping the Asparagus</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Buy asparagus with closed tips. The main thing to look for when buying asparagus is firm, compact, closed tips.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup> This means the asparagus is fresh and tasty.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-1.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 1.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/ab/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-1.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-1.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Also look for plump, straight stems for the healthiest asparagus.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup></li> \n    <li>If you have to get asparagus with an opened tip, you can try to revive it by soaking it in cold water.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Rinse the stalks in a colander. Prepping asparagus for cooking is very easy and only requires a quick rinse. Put the stalks in a colander and rinse them off under the faucet. Shake the colander to dry the vegetables off.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup> This should get rid of any dirt or debris stuck in the tips.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/ab/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-2.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re not using the asparagus right away, don’t wash them! Moisture can make them spoil in storage. Wait until you’re about to cook the asparagus to clean it.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Line up the stalks on a cutting board. Cutting the asparagus is also easy. Arrange them in a row on a cutting board. This way, you can cut them all in one pass.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-3.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 3.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/90/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-3.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-3.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Cut the asparagus just below the tip. Take a sharp knife and line it up just below the flowery tips of the asparagus. Press down to slice cleanly through all the stalks, then gather up the tips for cooking.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/cf/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-4.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Make sure you use a sharp knife to avoid tearing or crushing the asparagus.</li> \n    <li>The rest of the stalk is also edible, except for the very end, which is very tough and woody. You can use all of these cooking tips for the rest of the stalk too.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Asparagus-Tips&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Seasoning the Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Seasoning-the-Tips\">Seasoning the Tips</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Add salt and pepper for the most common seasonings. No matter how you cook the asparagus, salt and pepper are always a good addition. Sprinkle some onto the tips before serving for some extra flavor.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/ac/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-5.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you roast or grill the asparagus, it’s best to season them beforehand so the flavors cook into the tips.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Drizzle some olive oil for extra flavor. The earthy taste of olive oil goes great with asparagus. Try drizzling some on before serving, or tossing the asparagus and other veggies with some oil to add flavor.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/6d/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-6.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You could also use a different vegetable oil like canola instead.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup> It depends on your preference.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Add some lemon juice for a citrusy flavor. Citrus and asparagus go great together. Try squeezing some fresh lemon juice over the tips before serving.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/10/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-7.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You could also zest some lemon over the asparagus for a stronger flavor.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Sprinkle some Parmesan cheese on for some extra zest. You might not think of cheese when you think of asparagus, but it's a very popular flavoring that can really give the vegetable a kick. Try sprinkling some on before roasting or grilling, or adding it afterward before serving.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-8.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 8.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/38/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-8.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-8.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Give the asparagus some crunch with breadcrumbs. This is especially good if you're roasting, barbecuing, or frying the tips. Simply coat the asparagus with breadcrumbs, and any other seasons, before cooking to give them a nice, crunchy exterior.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-9.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 9.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/2b/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-9.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-9.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For extra flavor, you can use seasoned breadcrumbs.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Cook-Asparagus-Tips&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Cooking Options\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Cooking-Options\">Cooking Options</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Boil the asparagus tips for a simple recipe. This is one of the most common and easy ways to cook asparagus. Boil a pot of water, then put the asparagus tips in. Asparagus is usually ready in 5-8 minutes, depending on how tender you want them.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup> However, since you're only cooking the tips, you can shorten this time. Check on the asparagus after about 3 minutes.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-10.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 10.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c8/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-10.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-10.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Blanching is similar to boiling, but it keeps the asparagus crunchier. To blanch, bring a few inches of water to a rapid boil, then throw the asparagus in for about 30-60 seconds. After that, take them out and plunge them into ice water to stop the cooking process.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Steam-Asparagus\" title=\"Steam Asparagus\">Steam the asparagus</a> in on the stove or in the microwave. This is another simple and popular way to prep asparagus tips. Fill the bottom of a double boiler or steamer with about of water. Boil the water, then throw in the asparagus tips and cover the pot. Asparagus stalks usually cook in 5-8 minutes, but shorten that time since you're only cooking the tips.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/81/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-11.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You could also steam the asparagus in your microwave with a wet paper towel.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Asparagus\" title=\"Roast Asparagus\">Roast the tips</a> in the oven. If you prefer your asparagus a little crispy, then roasting the tips is a good choice. Preheat your oven to and arrange the asparagus on a baking sheet. Drizzle some oil over the tips and season with salt and pepper. The roasting time for asparagus stalks is 18-20 minutes.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup> Keep an eye on the asparagus, because the tips should cook faster than this.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-12.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 12.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/2c/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-12.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-12.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Don’t overlap any of the asparagus or they won’t all cook correctly.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Add the tips to a stir-fry dish. Heat 1-2 tbsp (5-10 ml) of oil in a skillet, then throw the asparagus tips in.<sup id=\"_ref-16\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 16\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-16\">[16]</a></sup> Keep the heat medium-high and stir the tips continuously for 3-5 minutes to cook the tips.<sup id=\"_ref-17\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 17\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-17\">[17]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-13.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 13.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b6/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-13.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-13.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For more flavor, use butter instead of oil.</li> \n    <li>It’s also easy to use the rest of the asparagus stalk in a stir-fry. Just cut them into small pieces about the same size as the tips and throw them in.</li> \n    <li>You could stir-fry the asparagus alone, or throw them in to a whole stir-fry dish and cook everything together.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Grill the tips for a crispier exterior. Grilled asparagus tips are a great side dish for a cookout. Simply put them on a pan and place it directly over a high heat. For whole stalks, cover the grill and wait about 5 minutes for the asparagus to get brown on one side. Then flip them over and cook for another 2-3 minutes.<sup id=\"_ref-18\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 18\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cook-Asparagus-Tips#_note-18\">[18]</a></sup> Shorten this time since you're only cooking tips.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-14.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Cook Asparagus Tips Step 14.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a6/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-14.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-14.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You might want to pre-season the tips with salt, pepper, olive oil, or any other seasonings you might want.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span 9063.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/38/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-8.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-8.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn72@2020_3/2020/10/12/17-04-49-743_6df9b674a10097e3.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/2b/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-9.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-9.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn27@2020_3/2020/10/12/17-04-48-240_fa8a144ededdf9e7.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c8/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-10.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-10.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn72@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-04-48-287_156bf22e06cb80ea.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/81/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-11.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-11.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn36@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-04-48-648_c19698452937a5b9.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/2c/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-12.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-12.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn3@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-04-50-095_7711f8496d0f7eae.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b6/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-13.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-13.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn56@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-49-648_0c8edc38c18093ca.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a6/Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-14.jpg/aid12120994-v4-728px-Cook-Asparagus-Tips-Step-14.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn56@2020_3/2020/10/12/17-04-48-376_d4e599dee3903546.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522267306},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:27","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:27","title":"How to Iron a Dress Shirt","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Ironing might feel like a chore to you, especially if you don't feel like you're very good at it. Luckily, while it might seem tough, ironing a shirt is no big deal. In just a few minutes, you can become an ironing master! Plug your iron in and get started, and your shirt will be looking crisp in no time. </p>\n <p><br /> </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Iron-a-Dress-Shirt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Iron-a-Dress-Shirt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Setting Up the Iron\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Setting-Up-the-Iron\">Setting Up the Iron</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Fill the iron with fresh tap water. In almost all cases, fresh water from your tap is fine for ironing. Fill the iron up before getting started.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup><br /><br />\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-1-Version-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Iron a Dress Shirt Step 1 Version 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/ac/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-1-Version-6.jpg/aid371599-v4-728px-Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-1-Version-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Some older advice said to use distilled water, but this isn’t necessary and might even damage the iron.</li> \n    <li>The one exception is if the tap water in your area is particularly hard, meaning it has a lot of dissolved minerals in it. In this case, mix the tap water with half distilled water.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Select a high heat setting for cotton shirts. Most dress shirts are made with cotton, so a high heat setting is best. This will give you a nice, crisp finish.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-2-Version-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Iron a Dress Shirt Step 2 Version 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f1/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-2-Version-6.jpg/aid371599-v4-728px-Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-2-Version-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Always check the care tag to confirm the material that the shirt is made from. The care tag may also give the ideal temperature setting for the iron.</li> \n    <li>Polyester, wool, and silk shirts can’t handle high heats, so make sure you set the heat lower if you have shirts made from these materials. Don't go any higher than the low or medium setting on your iron.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Set the iron to its highest steam setting. You’ll need plenty of steam for a good finish, so don’t be shy. Crank up the steam setting to high. This will smooth out your dress shirts nicely.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-3-Version-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Iron a Dress Shirt Step 3 Version 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/17/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-3-Version-6.jpg/aid371599-v4-728px-Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-3-Version-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Spritz all your shirts with a spray bottle before ironing. Damp shirts tend to smooth out better, and a little extra moisture helps really get rid of those wrinkles. Fill a spray bottle with clean tap water and spritz down all the spots you’re ironing first. This should give you a smoother finish.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can skip this step if your clothes are still damp from washing.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Iron-a-Dress-Shirt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Collar\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Collar\">Collar</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Pop the shirt collar and flatten it onto the ironing board. Take the shirt and flip the collar up. Press the back of the shirt down onto the ironing board in any spot so the front of the collar faces up. Flatten the collar out so it’s nice and even.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Some dress shirts have buttons holding the collar down, so make sure you undo these first.</li> \n    <li>Remember to unbutton the shirt too.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Slide the iron across the collar. Press the iron down against one side of the collar. Then apply gentle pressure and slide the iron smoothly from one side to the other to work out any wrinkles.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can make a few more passes if the collar still looks wrinkled, but 1 or 2 is usually enough.</li> \n    <li>Some say that you’ll get a better finish if you iron the front or back of the collar first.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup> There’s disagreement, so you can experiment to see if you notice a difference.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Flip the shirt and iron the other side of the collar. Once the front of the collar is nice and smooth, flip the shirt over. Flatten out the collar again, then pass over it with the iron. This way, both sides of your collar are crisp and smooth.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re having trouble getting any of the wrinkles out, try spritzing the collar with the spray bottle a bit more.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Iron-a-Dress-Shirt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Front and Back\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Front-and-Back\">Front and Back</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Flatten the buttoned side of the shirt onto the ironing board. Take the side of the shirt with the buttons and tuck the neck over the pointy part of the ironing board. Then press the shirt onto the ironing board, trying to stretch it out a bit lengthwise. Smooth it out so it’s nice and tight against the board.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Slide the iron from the outside of the shirt towards the buttons. Hold the iron so it points up toward the shirt collar. Press it down onto the shirt with gentle pressure, and work it horizontally from the outside to the inside toward the buttons. Stop when you reach the buttons. Continue working in this pattern until the side of the shirt is smooth.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Be careful not to hit any of the buttons with the iron or you could rip them off.</li> \n    <li>If the space in between the buttons is wrinkly, then carefully press the thin point of the iron into these spots.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Repeat the same motion on the other side of the shirt. When you’re done on the first side, flatten out the other side of the shirt onto the ironing board and tuck the neck over the pointed part of the board. Smooth out this side with the iron using the same motion as you used on the first side.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>On most dress shirts, the pocket is on the side without the buttons. Smooth over this very carefully so you don’t rip it.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Run the iron down the buttonhole section. This is the placket, the part with the buttonholes. You want this to look nice and crisp too. Press the iron down at the top of the placket near the neck. Then smoothly run it down the placket to flatten it out.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Don’t try this same motion on the other side with the buttons, or you might rip them off.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Flip the shirt and iron the back. Once you’re done with the front of the shirt, move on to the back. Flip it over and center the collar at the pointy edge of the ironing board. Tuck the collar over the pointy part to hold it in place. Flatten the shirt out, then slide the iron from the top of the shirt down. Work in even rows to avoid making any new wrinkles.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You could also do the back of the shirt first if you prefer. The order doesn’t matter.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Slide the shirt left or right to get any sections that couldn’t fit. You probably won’t be able to fit the whole back of the shirt onto the ironing board, so slide it to the side so you can reach the rest of it. First, slide it to the left and iron that section. Finally, slide it to the right and iron this part to finish up the back.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Finish up with the stitched section on the shoulders. This is the yoke, the boxy section on the back around the shoulders. Adjust the shirt so the whole yoke is sitting on the ironing board at any point. Slide the iron across it to work out any wrinkles.<sup id=\"_ref-16\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 16\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-16\">[16]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>It's common to miss this spot, and many people overlook it. Don't be one of them! Make sure your whole shirt is crisp and smooth.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Iron-a-Dress-Shirt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Sleeves and Cuffs\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Sleeves-and-Cuffs\">Sleeves and Cuffs</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Spread out the shirt cuffs and press them flat. Unbutton all the parts of the cuff and open them up. Then press the cuff flat onto the ironing board at any point, facing up.<sup id=\"_ref-17\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 17\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-17\">[17]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Iron the inside of the cuff first. This gives you a crisper finish. Slide the iron across the inside of the cuff from one side to the other.<sup id=\"_ref-18\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 18\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-18\">[18]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You might find it easier to just use the front edge of the iron for this. It fits into the cuff better.</li> \n    <li>Watch out for the buttons here too. You don't want to rip any parts of the shirt.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Flip the sleeve and iron the outside of the cuff. With the inside of the cuff done, flip the sleeve so you can reach the outside. Flatten out, the same way as you did with the inside. Then slide the iron across the cuff to smooth it out.<sup id=\"_ref-19\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 19\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-19\">[19]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Repeat the same steps for the other cuff.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Spread the sleeve out and iron it. Turn the shirt so the sleeve points down the length of the shirt. Stretch out one of the sleeves and press it down onto the ironing board. Make sure the sleeve is folded at the seam. Then work the iron from the top of the sleeve down until you reach the cuff.<sup id=\"_ref-20\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 20\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-20\">[20]</a></sup><br /><br />\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-18.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Iron a Dress Shirt Step 18.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/22/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-18.jpg/aid371599-v4-728px-Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-18.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If there are still some wrinkles left, work the iron across the sleeve to smooth them out.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Turn the sleeve and iron the other side. Finally, all that’s left is the other side of the sleeve. Flip the shirt over and flatten the sleeve out. Then gently run the iron down the sleeve to the cuff. If there are still wrinkles, then work the iron across the sleeve towards the seam as well.<sup id=\"_ref-21\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 21\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-21\">[21]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Repeat these steps for the last sleeve. Once you've successfully ironed one sleeve, the other one is no problem! Simply flip the shirt over and stretch out the sleeve down the ironing board. Give it a quick ironing and your shirt is all set to wear.<sup id=\"_ref-22\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 22\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-22\">[22]</a></sup><br /><br />\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-20.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Iron a Dress Shirt Step 20.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/3b/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-20.jpg/aid371599-v4-728px-Iron-a-Dress-Shirt-Step-20.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Iron-a-Dress-Shirt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Smooth, even strokes are best for a crisp finish. Try to avoid quick or jerky movements.<sup id=\"_ref-23\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 23\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Iron-a-Dress-Shirt#_note-23\">[23]</a></sup></li> \n  <li>Waist-height is usually the ideal setting for your ironing board.</li> \n  <li>If you aren’t wearing the shirt, then hang it right away so it stays wrinkle-free.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Iron-a-Dress-Shirt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Warnings\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Warnings\">Warnings</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Don’t leave the iron in one spot or you could burn the shirt.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Iron-a-Dress-Shirt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8\" title=\"Edit section: Video\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Video\">Video</span></h2> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span wikiHows\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Related-wikiHows\">Related wikiHows</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li><a target=\"_blank\"
