</li> \n  </ol>\n </div> \n</div>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 12 Oct 2020 16:00:00 +0000","feedId":44,"bgimg":"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/69/Play-a-Video-in-a-Zoom-Meeting-Step-1.jpg/aid12172625-v4-728px-Play-a-Video-in-a-Zoom-Meeting-Step-1.jpg","linkMd5":"769f1e75ccf62c985ee811204263bf58","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn11@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-04-27-631_48efa96775d74784.webp","destWidth":728,"destHeight":545,"sourceBytes":35304,"destBytes":19918,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/69/Play-a-Video-in-a-Zoom-Meeting-Step-1.jpg/aid12172625-v4-728px-Play-a-Video-in-a-Zoom-Meeting-Step-1.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn11@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-04-27-631_48efa96775d74784.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/ca/Play-a-Video-in-a-Zoom-Meeting-Step-2.jpg/aid12172625-v4-728px-Play-a-Video-in-a-Zoom-Meeting-Step-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn24@2020_6/2020/10/12/17-04-47-204_75aafefde2033492.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/61/Play-a-Video-in-a-Zoom-Meeting-Step-3.jpg/aid12172625-v4-728px-Play-a-Video-in-a-Zoom-Meeting-Step-3.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn48@2020_5/2020/10/12/17-04-50-679_698fa023990fa8f4.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/1e/Play-a-Video-in-a-Zoom-Meeting-Step-4.jpg/aid12172625-v4-728px-Play-a-Video-in-a-Zoom-Meeting-Step-4.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn8@2020_1/2020/10/12/17-04-49-454_a7725a65965d35f1.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/71/Play-a-Video-in-a-Zoom-Meeting-Step-5.jpg/aid12172625-v4-728px-Play-a-Video-in-a-Zoom-Meeting-Step-5.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn20@2020_3/2020/10/12/17-04-48-182_aa11b1e3da699133.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522267276},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:27","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:27","title":"How to Crochet a Potholder","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Potholders are a perfect project if you're new to crocheting or just want to use up some of your yarn. As long as you can make a chain and single crochet, you should be able to create a thick square that protects you from hot pots and pans. This double-thick potholder is worked around instead of back and forth so both layers form as you crochet. It's sometimes called a folded or magic potholder because it works up so quickly! </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Crochet-a-Potholder&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Crochet-a-Potholder&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Making a Foundation Chain\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Making-a-Foundation-Chain\">Making a Foundation Chain</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Choose worsted weight cotton yarn. You'll need a 4-ounce (113 g) skein of worsted weight yarn or #4 yarn like afghan or aran yarn. Look for yarn made from all cotton since acrylic yarn can melt if you set a hot pan on it.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Crochet-a-Potholder-Step-1.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Crochet a Potholder Step 1.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/17/Crochet-a-Potholder-Step-1.jpg/aid12137971-v4-728px-Crochet-a-Potholder-Step-1.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Pick a solid yarn or get multi-colored yarn for a vibrant potholder.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Make a slip knot. Pull a length of yarn and twist the end into a loop. Slide your thumb and forefinger into the loop and use them to grab the yarn tail. Hold the working yarn with your other hand so you can pull the tail through the loop near its center or near the loop-side of the tail. Gently pull the working yarn to close the loop around the tail as you pull it through to make another loop.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you're new to <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Slip-Knot\" title=\"Make a Slip Knot\">making slip knots</a>, practice a few times. To tell if you've correctly made a slip knot, keep pulling the yarn in opposite directions. The knot should come undone instead of tightening.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Slide the knot onto a size US G (5 mm) crochet hook. Slip the knot onto the crochet hook and pull the yarn until it's snug around the hook. Don't pull too tightly or you'll have a hard time making your foundation chain.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Make 35 chain stitches to create a foundation chain. Take the working yarn that's attached to the skein and wrap it once around your crochet hook. Bring the hook through the loop to make 1 chain. Then, repeat this to make a total of 35 chain stitches, which should be around long.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>This makes the foundation or bottom edge for your potholder.</li> \n    <li>Although gauge doesn't matter very much for this project, you may want to crochet tighter if your chain is longer than or make looser stitches if your chain is too short.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Crochet-a-Potholder&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Single-Crocheting the Potholder\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Single-Crocheting-the-Potholder\">Single-Crocheting the Potholder</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Make a single crochet (SC) into the foundation chain. Insert your hook into the chain stitch that's closest to the hook and wrap the yarn around it once. Bring the hook back through the chain so you have 2 loops on the hook. Wrap the yarn around the hook 1 more time and pull your hook through the 2 loops to create 1 single crochet stitch.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>The single crochet stitch is one of the fastest crochet stitches to work, so this potholder comes together quickly.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Single crochet until you reach the last stitch on the foundation. Keep making a single crochet stitch into each chain. Stop crocheting when there's just 1 chain left on the foundation.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>This means you'll make a total of 34 SC stitches on this side of the foundation chain.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Make 2 single crochet stitches in the last stitch to make a corner. Once you're at the last chain on the foundation, make a SC stitch. Then, insert your hook into the same chain stitch and make another SC stitch into it. This makes a slight curve that forms the corner of your potholder.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Single crochet every stitch along the other side of the chain. Now that you've curved the end of your foundation, you can crochet into the back loops of the chain. Make a SC stitch into the back of each stitch until you reach the other end of the row. You'll make 35 SC stitches along the back of the foundation chain. This completes the first full row of SC.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>It's really important that you don't join the rows and turn the work. Instead, remember to SC into the back loops.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Continue to SC back and forth until your potholder is an square. You don't need to make extra SC stitches in the corners since you've already established them. Just remember to keep making SC stitches into the stitches of the SC row immediately before it, rather than into the chain stitches. Depending on your tension, you'll need to knit around 40 rows of SC with 71 stitches each. When your potholder is at least square, work to the end of the last row you'd like to complete.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>This makes 2 layers of fabric, which form the double-thick potholder.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Crochet-a-Potholder&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Finishing Your Potholder\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Finishing-Your-Potholder\">Finishing Your Potholder</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Make 7 chain stitches to form a hanging loop. When you reach the corner and your potholder is as big as you like, make 7 chain stitches. This makes a short length of fabric that you'll use to make a loop for hanging up your potholder when you're not using it.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Attach the loop to the potholder with a slip stitch. Keep the last loop of your chain on your hook and push your hook into the corner of your potholder. To join the loop to the potholder, grab the working yarn with your hook. Pull it through the loop and then pull it through the stitch on your hook.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you don't want your potholder to have a hanging loop, just skip these steps and tie off your working yarn.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Cut a yarn tail and tie off the yarn. Leave a long yarn tail that you can use to sew the top of the potholder closed. Before you sew it closed, however, bring the yarn through your last stitch and make a knot.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you forget to leave a long yarn tail, just tie a length of yarn to the end of your yarn tail and use it to sew the potholder shut.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Thread a tapestry needle and whipstitch the top edges closed. Insert the needle through the stitch that's closest to the hanging loop and push it through the opposite stitch on the other edge of the potholder. Pull the yarn and insert the needle through the next stitch. Continue to <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Whipstitch\" title=\"Whipstitch\">whipstitch</a> until you reach the end. Then, tie off the yarn and use your hook to pull the tail into the center of the potholder.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you feel more comfortable making the slip stitch, use a tapestry needle to slip stitch between the stitches on the edges of the potholder to join them.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Crochet-a-Potholder&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Creating a potholder is great crocheting practice and they make great gifts!</li> \n  <li>It's really important to sew a double-thick potholder instead of a single-layer one since the extra layer protects you from getting burned.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Crochet-a-Potholder&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Things You'll Need\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span id=\"Things-You'll-Need\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Things-You.27ll-Need\">Things You'll Need</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>4-ounce (113 g) skein of worsted weight yarn</li> \n  <li>Size US G (5 mm) crochet hook</li> \n  <li>Scissors</li> \n  <li>Tapestry or darning needle</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Crochet-a-Potholder&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: References\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"References\">References</span></h2>\n <div class=\"mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns\">\n  <ol class=\"references\"> \n   <li id=\"_note-1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_ref-1\">↑</a> <span class=\"reference-text\"><a href=\"https://youtu.be/bVRKivE1WxA?t=244\">https://youtu.be/bVRKivE1WxA?t=244</a></span> </li> \n   <li id=\"_note-9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://extension.usu.edu/sewing/ou-files/crocheting.pdf\">https://extension.usu.edu/sewing/ou-files/crocheting.pdf</a></span> </li> \n   <li id=\"_note-10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_ref-10\">↑</a> <span class=\"reference-text\"><a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"https://extension.usu.edu/sewing/ou-files/crocheting.pdf\">https://extension.usu.edu/sewing/ou-files/crocheting.pdf</a></span> </li> \n   <li id=\"_note-11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_ref-12\">↑</a> <span class=\"reference-text\"><a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"https://youtu.be/Mm2FrLdF6MI?t=369\">https://youtu.be/Mm2FrLdF6MI?t=369</a></span> </li> \n   <li id=\"_note-13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Crochet-a-Potholder#_ref-13\">↑</a> <span class=\"reference-text\"><a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"https://youtu.be/Mm2FrLdF6MI?t=438\">https://youtu.be/Mm2FrLdF6MI?t=438</a></span> </li> \n  </ol>\n </div> \n</div>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sun, 11 Oct 2020 00:00:00 +0000","feedId":44,"bgimg":"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/17/Crochet-a-Potholder-Step-1.jpg/aid12137971-v4-728px-Crochet-a-Potholder-Step-1.jpg","linkMd5":"ca057dd7b6d355e702e9851c4aeb73de","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn19@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-31-491_a9ff4edb9287a752.webp","destWidth":728,"destHeight":410,"sourceBytes":36293,"destBytes":20346,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/17/Crochet-a-Potholder-Step-1.jpg/aid12137971-v4-728px-Crochet-a-Potholder-Step-1.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn19@2020_2/2020/10/12/17-04-31-491_a9ff4edb9287a752.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602522267326},{"createdTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:27","updatedTime":"2020-10-13 01:04:27","title":"How to Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Rabbits are cute, cuddly, and make great pets! Because of their size and quiet habits, rabbits are actually perfect if you live in an apartment. While <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Care-for-a-Rabbit\" title=\"Care for a Rabbit\">caring for a rabbit</a> is similar whether you live in a house or apartment, there are a few extra steps you’ll need to take to make sure your rabbit stays healthy and doesn’t damage anything. As long as you take these precautions, then your rabbit will stay happy for years to come! </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Rabbit-Proofing Your Apartment\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Rabbit-Proofing-Your-Apartment\">Rabbit-Proofing Your Apartment</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Confirm that your apartment allows rabbits. Whether you’re moving to a new place or have already moved in, you always need to check your landlord’s animal rules before getting a pet. This is especially important with rabbits, because they love to chew and can cause some serious damage for such a small animal. Confirm that rabbits are allowed before getting one.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-1-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 1 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/97/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-1-Version-2.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-1-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Don’t assume that an apartment allows rabbits just because it allows dogs and cats. Many landlords put rabbits in a different category, so asking is the best bet.</li> \n    <li>If a landlord doesn’t explicitly say that they don’t allow pets and you aren’t sure, then make an appointment to see the place and give a good impression before mentioning your pet. They might be more willing to make an exception if you seem like a good tenant.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Put plastic carpet protectors in room corners if you have carpeting. Rabbits love to dig, and they have a habit of digging into carpets in corners. If you do have carpets, put down plastic carpet protectors in the corners, the same type you'd use under a computer chair or desk.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-2-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 2 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/4b/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-2-Version-2.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-2-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You could also just block off carpeted areas instead.</li> \n    <li>Make sure you put some hay in your rabbit’s enclosure so it can dig there. This can distract it from digging at carpets.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Use baseboard covers to protect your walls. Baseboards are the perfect height for rabbits to chew on, and their little teeth can do some real damage. Luckily, hardware stores sell baseboard covers that can prevent this. Get some of these and install them over the baseboards to protect your walls.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-3-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 3 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/2a/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-3-Version-2.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-3-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Using furniture or boxes to block off the baseboards is another option, but it might not be practical to do this through your whole apartment.</li> \n    <li>You could also use something like bitter apple spray to make walls and wood furniture taste bad. This might stop your rabbit from chewing on them.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Block off areas with wires so your rabbit can’t chew on them. Rabbits have a habit of chewing on wires, which can not only cut your power, but could hurt your rabbit. Go through your apartment and try to block off spots that have a lot of wires. Common spots are behind your TV, on your desk, near your router, and around any appliances. If you can’t block off these areas, try to raise the wires up so your rabbit can’t reach them.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 4 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/74/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-4-Version-2.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can get little plastic attachments at most hardware or electronics stores to stick wires to your walls and raise them up. Tape also works.</li> \n    <li>Make sure you check your entire apartment to find any wires that you might’ve missed. Your rabbit can fit into small spaces and might uncover some wires to chew on.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Wrap wires in coating to protect them. Whether you can’t block off all your wires or you just want to be extra careful, protective coating can also stop your rabbit from biting through them. Try getting metal or plastic coatings from an electronics store and wrapping them around your wires for an extra layer of protection.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-5-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 5 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b3/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-5-Version-2.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-5-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>These coatings are just a precaution, and your rabbit could still bite through them with some extra work. Make sure you keep an eye on your rabbit and stop them from biting any wires.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Raise houseplants so your rabbit can’t reach them. Most houseplants are toxic to rabbits, but this won’t stop your rabbit from trying to eat them. Make sure your raise all your houseplants high enough so your rabbit can’t reach them at all.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-6-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 6 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/93/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-6-Version-2.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-6-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Setting Up Your Rabbit’s Space\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span id=\"Setting-Up-Your-Rabbit’s-Space\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Setting-Up-Your-Rabbit.E2.80.99s-Space\">Setting Up Your Rabbit’s Space</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Pick a roomy, quiet spot for your rabbit’s living area. Even if you’re going to let your rabbit roam the apartment, it’s best for rabbits to have a home base to rest, eat, use the bathroom, and play. Start by choosing a roomy spot large enough to set up a big cage or enclosure. Make sure it’s a quiet spot, but not too far away from everyone else so your rabbit doesn’t feel lonely.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-7-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 7 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/be/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-7-Version-2.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-7-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re in a small apartment, you might have to rearrange some furniture to make room.</li> \n    <li>If you have enough space, you could make a whole room your rabbit’s living area. This way, you can just focus on rabbit-proofing that room instead of your whole apartment.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Keep your rabbit in a cool spot away from direct sunlight. Make sure your rabbit's living space is cool and away from any heating vents, since they can overheat easily. Also make sure the area doesn't get any direct sunlight.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup> You might have to use shades to block sunlight and keep your rabbit comfortable.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-8-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 8 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/ba/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-8-Version-2.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-8-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Any drafts could make your rabbit uncomfortable, so make sure to close any vents or set up the living area out of their paths.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Set up a <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Set-up-a-Rabbit-Cage\" title=\"Set up a Rabbit Cage\">cage or pen</a> for your rabbit. In general, get housing that’s at least 4 times longer than your rabbit and twice as wide, but bigger is better because your rabbit will grow.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup> You can use either a large cage designed for rabbits or a gate to create an enclosure.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-9-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 9 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/8f/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-9-Version-2.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-9-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You could keep your rabbit penned in their housing most of the time, which makes protecting your apartment easier. That way, you can easily watch them while they’re running around and stop them from chewing anything.</li> \n    <li>Make sure any housing you use for your rabbit has flat flooring. Wire flooring is bad for their feet and they might dig into carpeting.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Include food and water in the rabbit’s cage. Rabbits like to eat in their living area, so make sure to set these up as well. Put your rabbit’s food bowl in the cage or enclosure, and hang their water bottle so they can drink whenever they want.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-10-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 10 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/bf/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-10-Version-2.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-10-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>This is important whether you have a caged or free-roam rabbit. Leave their food and water in their normal living area.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Put a litter area in the rabbit’s pen. Rabbits can be <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Litter-Train-a-Rabbit\" title=\"Litter Train a Rabbit\">house-trained</a>, which is very important for keeping one in your apartment. Setting up a litter area in your rabbit’s pen is very easy. Just put some crumpled up newspaper in a pan for your rabbit to use.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/70/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-11.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Make sure you clean the litter area daily.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup></li> \n    <li>Don’t use wood chips or kitty litter in your rabbit’s litter area. These can be toxic to rabbits.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rabbit-Cage\" title=\"Clean a Rabbit Cage\">Clean your rabbit's living area</a> weekly. Rabbits tend to be clean, but their living areas will inevitably get messy and smelly. Hair, old straw, and food bits can build up fast. Once or twice a week, do a full cage cleaning. Scoop out any old food or hair and wash the floor with soap and water.<sup id=\"_ref-16\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 16\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-16\">[16]</a></sup> Put fresh straw, cardboard, and newspaper in the cage and let it dry before letting your rabbit back in.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-12.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 12.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/75/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-12.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-12.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can let your rabbit roam or put them in another cage while you're cleaning.</li> \n    <li>Clean the area around the cage too, especially if it's carpeted. Vacuum and sweep any hairs, food, or straw so it doesn't start smelling.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Caring for Your Rabbit\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Caring-for-Your-Rabbit\">Caring for Your Rabbit</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Spay or neuter your rabbit. Fixing your rabbit solves a lot of behavioral issues like chewing and aggression, and it also makes house-training easier. In general, you should fix your rabbit between 3 1/2 and 6 months old, so visit a vet for the right procedure.<sup id=\"_ref-17\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 17\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-17\">[17]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-13.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 13.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e7/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-13.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-13.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If your landlord is on the fence about letting you keep a rabbit, emphasizing that neutering solves many issues could help convince them.<sup id=\"_ref-18\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 18\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-18\">[18]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Cut-a-Rabbit%27s-Claws\" title=\"Cut a Rabbit's Claws\">Trim your rabbit’s nails</a> regularly. If your rabbit has long nails, they’re more likely to damage your walls, floors, and carpets. Inspect your rabbit’s nails regularly and give them a trim if they’re long.<sup id=\"_ref-19\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 19\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-19\">[19]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-14.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 14.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b9/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-14.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-14.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>In general, a monthly trim is perfect. As soon as the nail starts curving, it needs to be clipped.</li> \n    <li>If you don’t know how to cut your rabbit’s nails, your vet can show you.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Give your rabbit plenty of toys to chew on. Rabbits are more likely to chew on furniture and walls if they’re bored. Make sure your rabbit has plenty of chew toys to keep them busy. This way, you can cut down on the amount of chewing they do around your apartment.<sup id=\"_ref-20\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 20\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-20\">[20]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-15.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 15.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a0/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-15.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-15.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can get rabbit chew toys from a pet store. Rabbits also like chewing on cardboard, so try using some old boxes or toilet paper tubes for an inexpensive option.</li> \n    <li>Rabbits also love to play with non-toxic baby toys, so you can get some of these too.<sup id=\"_ref-21\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 21\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-21\">[21]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Exercise-Your-Rabbit\" title=\"Exercise Your Rabbit\">Let your rabbit exercise</a> for at least 3 hours a day. While they're tiny, rabbits are energetic animals and need to move around a lot to stay in shape. In general, they need at least 3 hours of exercise each day, so let yours out of its enclosure every day to move around. Rabbits exercise by hopping, chewing, playing with toys, and just generally exploring, so your rabbit should be able to take care of itself once you let it roam a little.<sup id=\"_ref-22\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 22\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-22\">[22]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-16.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 16.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/d9/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-16.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-16.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>This might be a little tougher in an apartment, but you don't need much room. As long as your rabbit has enough time and space to hop around, then it should be able to get plenty of exercise.</li> \n    <li>Keep an eye on your rabbit while it's roaming. Make sure it stays away from any wires, windows, or your front door.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Spend time with your rabbit so it stays happy. Rabbits need attention just like any other pet. Play with your rabbit and spend time with it every day. This keeps them happy and social.<sup id=\"_ref-23\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 23\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-23\">[23]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-17.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 17.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/da/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-17.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-17.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Rabbits don’t usually like being picked up, so don’t do this too much. You could let them sit or lay next to you while you’re on your couch to enjoy some connection instead.</li> \n    <li>Rabbits are happy in groups, so you might want to consider getting another one so your rabbit has a friend. However, only do this if you’re sure you can take care of more than one rabbit.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Protect your rabbit from other pets. While rabbits can definitely live together with other pets, you have to make sure your rabbit is protected at all times. Dogs or cats are natural hunters, and might go after your rabbit if they aren't introduced properly. Make sure the rabbit's living area is totally safe from other pets and they can't get in there. When you're letting your rabbit roam, keep an eye on all your pets so no accidents happen.<sup id=\"_ref-24\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 24\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment#_note-24\">[24]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-18.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Keep a Rabbit in an Apartment Step 18.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e4/Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-18.jpg/aid4504132-v4-728px-Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment-Step-18.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If possible, make sure your other pets are well-trained and respond to commands before adding a rabbit into the mix. This should prevent any problems.</li> \n    <li>Rabbits are sensitive to loud noises, so a barking dog could spook yours. If your dog starts barking, try to get it to quiet down.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Warnings\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Warnings\">Warnings</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>You might think rabbits are low-maintenance pets, but they require just as much work as any other pet. Be sure you're ready for the commitment if you're considering getting one.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Keep-a-Rabbit-in-an-Apartment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Related wikiHows\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Related-wikiHows\">Related wikiHows</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li><a target=\"_blank\"
